Title: Media Act 2024
Date: 2024-10-23
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2024/15

## Media Act 2024

      B e it enacted  by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Public service television

#### The public service remit for television

##### Reports on the fulfilment of the public service remit

1

1.1

Section 264 of the Communications Act 2003 (OFCOM reports on the fulfilment of
the public service remit) is amended as follows.

1.2

For subsections (3) to (8) (OFCOM’s review and reporting obligations and the
purposes of public service television broadcasting in the United Kingdom)
substitute—

1.2.3

The review and reporting obligations for a period are—

1.2.3.a

an obligation to carry out a review of the extent to which the public service
remit for television in the United Kingdom has, during that period, been
fulfilled by the public service broadcasters (taking them all together over
the period as a whole); and

1.2.3.b

an obligation, with a view to maintaining and strengthening the quality of the
audiovisual content made available in order to fulfil the public service remit
for television in the United Kingdom, to prepare a report on the matters found
in the review.

1.2.4

The public service remit for television in the United Kingdom is fulfilled
where the public service broadcasters (taken together) make available a broad
range of audiovisual content—

1.2.4.a

in a manner which, taking into account when and how their relevant audiovisual
services are received or accessed, is likely to meet the needs and satisfy the
interests of as many different audiences as practicable, and

1.2.4.b

which meets the needs and satisfies the interests of as many different
available audiences as practicable as regards the nature of the audiovisual
content made available and the subject-matters covered by it,

and that range of audiovisual content includes material satisfying the
requirements in  subsection (5)  and itself satisfies the requirement in
subsection (6) .

1.2.5

The requirements in this subsection are—

1.2.5.a

that the audiovisual content made available by the public service broadcasters
(taken together) provides, to the extent that is appropriate for facilitating
civic understanding and fair and well-informed debate on news and current
affairs, a comprehensive and authoritative coverage of news and current
affairs—

1.2.5.a.i

in, and in the different parts of, the United Kingdom, and

1.2.5.a.ii

from around the world;

1.2.5.b

that the audiovisual content made available by the public service broadcasters
(taken together) comprises a public service for the dissemination of
information and for the provision of education and entertainment, which
includes what appears to OFCOM to be—

1.2.5.b.i

a sufficient quantity of audiovisual content that reflects the lives and
concerns of different communities and cultural interests and traditions within
the United Kingdom, and locally in different parts of the United Kingdom, and

1.2.5.b.ii

a sufficient quantity of audiovisual content that is in, or mainly in, a
recognised regional or minority language;

1.2.5.c

that the audiovisual content made available by the public service broadcasters
(taken together) includes an appropriate range and quantity of audiovisual
content, contained in original productions, that—

1.2.5.c.i

reflects the lives and concerns of children and young people in the United
Kingdom,

1.2.5.c.ii

is of an educational nature, and

1.2.5.c.iii

helps them to understand the world around them; and

1.2.5.d

that the audiovisual content made available by the public service broadcasters
(taken together) includes—

1.2.5.d.i

an appropriate range of independent productions with an appropriate combined
duration,

1.2.5.d.ii

an appropriate range of original productions with an appropriate combined
duration, and

1.2.5.d.iii

so far as the audiovisual content consists of programmes made in the United
Kingdom, an appropriate range of programmes made outside the M25 area with an
appropriate combined duration.

1.2.6

The requirement in this subsection is that the range of genres of audiovisual
content made available by the public service broadcasters (taken together)
constitutes an appropriate range of genres.

1.2.7

Particular audiovisual content made available by a public service broadcaster
is not to be taken into account for the purpose of determining the extent to
which the public service remit for television in the United Kingdom is
fulfilled unless the broadcaster has taken steps to ensure that the
audiovisual content in question may be received or accessed in accordance with
subsection (8)  by so much of the broadcaster’s intended audience as is
reasonably practicable.

1.2.8

Audiovisual content may be received or accessed in accordance with this
subsection if—

1.2.8.a

the audiovisual content, and

1.2.8.b

the relevant audiovisual service by means of which the audiovisual content is
provided,

may be received or accessed in intelligible form and free of charge.

1.2.8A

Any requirement to pay sums in accordance with regulations under section 365
is to be disregarded for the purpose of determining whether audiovisual
content may be received or accessed in accordance with  subsection (8) .

1.2.8B

Particular audiovisual content made available by a public service broadcaster
by means of an on-demand programme service or a non-UK on-demand programme
service is not to be taken into account for the purpose of determining the
extent to which the public service remit for television in the United Kingdom
is fulfilled unless the audiovisual content in question is available for a
period of not less than 30 days beginning with the day on which that content
is first made available for viewing.

1.2.8C

Subsection  (8B)  does not apply to news programmes or programmes containing
coverage of sporting events that are made available by a public service
broadcaster by means of an on-demand programme service or a non-UK on-demand
programme service.

1.2.8D

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  subsection (8B)  so as to
substitute a different period for the period for the time being specified
there.

1.2.8E

In carrying out a review under this section OFCOM must consider—

1.2.8E.a

the costs to public service broadcasters of fulfilling the public service
remit for television in the United Kingdom;

1.2.8E.b

the sources of income available to them for meeting those costs.

1.2.8F

Every report under this section must—

1.2.8F.a

specify, and comment on, whatever changes appear to OFCOM to have occurred,
during the period to which the report relates, in the extent to which the
public service remit for television in the United Kingdom has been fulfilled;

1.2.8F.b

specify, and comment on, whatever changes appear to OFCOM to have occurred,
during that period, in the manner in which that remit is fulfilled;

1.2.8F.c

set out the findings of OFCOM on their consideration of the matters mentioned
in  subsection (8E)  and any conclusions they have arrived at in relation to
those findings; and

1.2.8F.d

set out OFCOM’s conclusions on the current state of the audiovisual content
made available by public service broadcasters in order to fulfil the public
service remit for television in the United Kingdom.

1.3

After subsection (10) insert—

1.3.10A

Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must
consult OFCOM.

1.3.10B

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this section may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

1.4

For subsection (11) substitute—

1.4.11

The following are relevant audiovisual services for the purposes of this
section—

1.4.11.a

a television broadcasting service;

1.4.11.b

a television licensable content service;

1.4.11.c

a digital television programme service;

1.4.11.d

an on-demand programme service;

1.4.11.e

a non-UK on-demand programme service;

1.4.11.f

a service, other than a service referred to in any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (e)
, which falls within  subsection (11A) .

1.4.11A

A service falls within this subsection if it is a service, or a dissociable
section of a service, which has the following characteristics—

1.4.11A.a

its principal purpose is the provision of programmes,

1.4.11A.b

the programmes which it provides are accessed by viewers by means of the
internet,

1.4.11A.c

there is a person who has general control over which programmes are comprised
in the service or the dissociable section of the service (whether or not the
person has control of the content of individual programmes or the distribution
of the service), and

1.4.11A.d

the service or the dissociable section of the service is available for use by
members of the public in all or part of the United Kingdom.

1.4.11B

The services that are to be taken for the purposes of  subsection (11A) (d)
to be available for use by members of the public include any service which—

1.4.11B.a

is made available for use only to persons who subscribe to the service
(whether for a period or in relation to a particular occasion) or who
otherwise request its provision, but

1.4.11B.b

is a service the facility of subscribing to which, or otherwise requesting its
provision, is offered or made available to members of the public.

1.5

For subsection (13) substitute—

1.5.13

For the purposes of this section, audiovisual content is made available by a
public service broadcaster if—

1.5.13.a

it is provided by means of a relevant audiovisual service provided by the
broadcaster, or

1.5.13.b

it is provided by means of a relevant audiovisual service provided by another
person, under arrangements made between the broadcaster and that other person.

1.5.14

In the case of a service falling within  subsection (11) (f) , the person, and
the only person, who is to be treated for the purposes of this section as
providing the service is the person described in  subsection (11A) (c) ; and
section 362(3) applies in relation to such a service as it applies in relation
to a service referred to in section 362(2).

1.5.15

In this section, a reference to the provision of an on-demand programme
service or a non-UK on-demand programme service is to be read in accordance
with section 368R(5) and (6).

1.5.16

In this section—

      “ audiovisual content ” means the programmes, other than advertisements,
included in a relevant audiovisual service;           “ children ” means
persons under the age of 18;           “ independent production ”—         in
relation to the provider of a licensed public service channel, has the same
meaning as in section 277;           in relation to the BBC, has the same
meaning as in paragraph 1 of Schedule 12;           in relation to S4C, has
the same meaning as in paragraph 7 of Schedule 12;                 “ intended
audience ” means—         in relation to the provider of a Channel 3 service
provided for an area of the United Kingdom, members of the public in that
area;           in relation to any other public service broadcaster, members
of the public in the United Kingdom;                 “ original production ”—
in relation to the provider of a licensed public service channel, has the same
meaning as in section 278;           in relation to the BBC, has the meaning
given by the BBC Charter and Agreement;           in relation to S4C, has the
same meaning as in paragraph 8 of Schedule 12;                 “ programme ”
means any programme (with or without sounds) which consists of moving or still
images or of legible text or of a combination of those things;           “
recognised regional or minority language ” means Welsh, the Gaelic language as
spoken in Scotland, Irish, Scots, Ulster Scots or Cornish.

##### OFCOM reports: wider review and reporting obligations

2

2.1

Section 264A of the Communications Act 2003 (OFCOM reports: wider review and
reporting obligations) is amended as follows.

2.2

In subsection (1), for “public service objectives” substitute  “public service
requirements” .

2.3

In subsection (2)(b) and (c), for “objectives” substitute  “requirements” .

2.4

For subsections (3) and (4) substitute—

2.4.3

“The public service requirements” are the requirements set out in paragraphs
(a)  to  (d)  of section 264 (5) , as modified by subsection (4).

2.4.4

Section 264 (5)  has effect for the purposes of subsection (3) as if
references to audiovisual content made available by the public service
broadcasters, or to programmes included in that content, were references to
material included in media services.

2.5

In subsection (5), in the definition of “media services”, after paragraph (b)
(and before the “and” following it) insert—

2.5.ba

non-UK on-demand programme services,

.

##### Public service remits of licensed providers

3

3.1

Section 265 of the Communications Act 2003 (licence conditions for a licensed
public service channel to include fulfilling public service remits) is amended
as follows.

3.2

For subsection (2) (public service remit for Channel 3 services and Channel 5)
substitute—

3.2.2

The public service remit for every Channel 3 service and for Channel 5 is to
make available a range of high quality and diverse audiovisual content—

3.2.2.a

which is all capable of being taken into account for the purpose of
determining the extent to which the public service remit for television in the
United Kingdom is fulfilled (see section 264 (7)  to  (8C) ), and

3.2.2.b

which, considered as a whole, constitutes an adequate contribution to the
fulfilment of that remit.

3.3

For subsection (3) (public service remit for Channel 4) substitute—

3.3.3

The public service remit for Channel 4 is to make available a broad range of
high quality and diverse audiovisual content—

3.3.3.a

which, in particular—

3.3.3.a.i

demonstrates innovation, experiment and creativity in the form and content of
programmes,

3.3.3.a.ii

appeals to the tastes and interests of a culturally diverse society,

3.3.3.a.iii

includes a significant quantity and range of programmes of an educational
nature and other programmes of educative value, and

3.3.3.a.iv

exhibits a distinctive character,

3.3.3.b

which is all capable of being taken into account for the purpose of
determining the extent to which the public service remit for television in the
United Kingdom is fulfilled, and

3.3.3.c

which, considered as a whole, constitutes an adequate contribution to the
fulfilment of that remit.

3.4

After subsection (5) insert—

3.4.6

In this section, a reference to making available audiovisual content, in
relation to a licensed public service channel, is a reference to the provider
of that channel making available audiovisual content.

3.4.7

Section 264 (13)  applies for the purposes of this section as it applies for
the purposes of section 264.

##### Statements of programme policy

4

4.1

Section 266 of the Communications Act 2003 (statements of programme policy for
Channel 3 services, Channel 4 and Channel 5) is amended as follows.

4.2

After subsection (2) insert—

4.2.2A

The condition must require such proposals—

4.2.2A.a

to state whether two or more relevant audiovisual services (including the
channel) are proposed to be used to fulfil the public service remit for the
channel, and

4.2.2A.b

if so, to identify, in relation to each of the relevant audiovisual services,
its proposed contribution to the fulfilment of the remit.

4.3

In subsection (5), for “section 264(4) and (6)” substitute  “section 264 (4)
to  (6) ” .

##### Changes of programme policy

5

In section 267 of the Communications Act 2003 (changes of programme policy for
Channel 3 services, Channel 4 and Channel 5), in subsection (4), for “which
the channel would” substitute

which—

5.a

the channel, or

5.b

any other relevant audiovisual service which is being used to fulfil the
public service remit for the channel,

would

.

##### Enforcement of public service remits

6

6.1

Section 270 of the Communications Act 2003 (enforcement of public service
remits) is amended as follows.

6.2

In subsection (1)—

6.2.a

in paragraph (a), after “failed” insert  “, in any respect,” ;

6.2.b

omit paragraph (b) and the “or” before it.

6.3

In subsection (3), after paragraph (c) insert—

6.3.ca

the record of the provider as regards compliance with duties under Part 4A
(on-demand programme services);

.

6.4

After subsection (4) insert—

6.4.4A

Where the provider’s latest statement of programme policy states that one or
more relevant audiovisual services other than the provider’s channel will be
used to fulfil the public service remit for the channel, a direction given
under this section may make provision with respect to that service or any of
those services.

6.5

In subsection (6)(b), omit the words from “or adequately” to “Kingdom”.

6.6

In subsection (7)(b), omit sub-paragraph (ii) and the “and” before it.

6.7

After subsection (7) insert—

6.7.7A

Where the provider’s latest statement of programme policy states that one or
more relevant audiovisual services other than the provider’s channel will be
used to fulfil the public service remit for the channel, specific conditions
inserted into the provider’s licence under subsection (7) may make provision
with respect to that service or any of those services.

(4)  to  (8C) ).

;

7.b

omit paragraph (c).

#### Programming quotas for public service television

##### Quotas: independent productions

8

8.1

Section 277 of the Communications Act 2003 (programming quotas for independent
productions) is amended as follows.

8.2

For subsection (1) substitute—

8.2.1

The regulatory regime for every licensed public service channel includes the
conditions that OFCOM consider appropriate for securing that in each year—

8.2.1.a

the provider of the licensed public service channel makes available qualifying
audiovisual content that includes a range and diversity of independent
productions commissioned in accordance with the provider’s commissioning code,
and

8.2.1.b

the duration (in total) of those independent productions is at least the
number of hours specified by order of the Secretary of State.

8.3

In subsection (2), omit paragraph (a).

8.4

Omit subsection (3).

8.5

In subsection (5), for the words from “, in each year” to the end of the
subsection substitute

—

8.5.a

in each year, the provider of the licensed public service channel makes
available qualifying audiovisual content that includes a range and diversity
of independent productions commissioned in accordance with the provider’s
commissioning code, and

8.5.b

the cost (in total) of the acquisition of those independent productions is at
least the amount specified in the order.

8.6

In subsection (8), in paragraph (b), for “the percentage” substitute  “the
number of hours or (as the case may be) the amount” .

8.7

Omit subsection (9).

8.8

Omit subsection (10).

8.9

After subsection (12) insert—

8.9.12A

If a draft of a statutory instrument containing an order under this section
would, apart from this subsection, be treated for the purposes of the standing
orders of either House of Parliament as a hybrid instrument, it is to proceed
in that House as if it were not such an instrument.

8.10

In subsection (13)—

8.10.a

after the definition of “acquisition” insert—

      “ commissioning code ”, in relation to a provider, means the code of
practice drawn up by the provider in pursuance of conditions included in the
provider’s licence by virtue of section 285;

;

8.10.b

omit the definition of “programming budget” and the word “and” before it.

8.11

After subsection (13) insert—

8.11.14

See also sections  278B  and  278C  (which make further provision for the
interpretation of this section etc).

##### Quotas: original productions

9

9.1

Section 278 of the Communications Act 2003 (programming quotas for original
productions) is amended as follows.

9.2

For subsection (1) substitute—

9.2.1

The regulatory regime for every licensed public service channel includes the
conditions that OFCOM consider appropriate for securing that in each year—

9.2.1.a

the provider of the licensed public service channel makes available qualifying
audiovisual content that includes a range of original productions,

9.2.1.b

the duration (in total) of those original productions is at least the number
of hours that OFCOM consider appropriate, and

9.2.1.c

if OFCOM consider it appropriate, the additional peak viewing time objective
described in  subsection (1A)  is met.

9.2.1A

The additional peak viewing time objective is that (out of the number of hours
determined by OFCOM for the purposes of  subsection (1) (b) ) at least the
number of hours that OFCOM consider appropriate is allocated to the
broadcasting of original productions included in the channel at peak viewing
times.

9.3

Omit subsections (2) and (3).

9.4

After subsection (7) insert—

9.4.7A

An order under subsection (6) may—

9.4.7A.a

authorise OFCOM to provide in a condition included in a licence by virtue of
this section that original productions of a description specified in the
licence may not be counted towards meeting the condition;

9.4.7A.b

require OFCOM to prepare and publish guidance about the determination of
whether an original production falls within a description included in a
licence by virtue of paragraph (a);

9.4.7A.c

authorise OFCOM to provide in a condition included in a licence by virtue of
this section that the holder of the licence must have regard to that guidance.

9.5

After subsection (11) insert—

9.5.12

See also sections  278B  and  278C  (which make further provision for the
interpretation of this section etc).

##### Power to create additional quotas for qualifying audiovisual content

10

After section 278 of the Communications Act 2003 insert—

######### Additional quotas for qualifying audiovisual content

10.278A

10.278A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations specify a description of qualifying
audiovisual content for the purposes of this section if—

10.278A.1.a

the Secretary of State considers that qualifying audiovisual content of that
description is not being made available by the providers of licensed public
service channels (taken together) to the extent that is appropriate, and

10.278A.1.b

subsection  (3)  applies.

10.278A.2

The descriptions that may be specified under  subsection (1)  include
descriptions that are framed in part by reference to the qualifying
audiovisual service by means of which the content is made available.

10.278A.3

This subsection applies where OFCOM have made a recommendation for the making
of the regulations in their most recent report under section 229 or 264.

10.278A.4

Where the Secretary of State makes regulations under  subsection (1) , the
regulatory regime for every licensed public service channel includes the
conditions that OFCOM consider appropriate for securing that in each year—

10.278A.4.a

the provider of the licensed public service channel makes available qualifying
audiovisual content that includes content of the description specified in the
regulations, and

10.278A.4.b

the duration (in total) of content of that description is at least the number
of hours that OFCOM consider appropriate.

10.278A.5

Before including a recommendation for the making of regulations under
subsection (1)  in a report under section 229 or 264, OFCOM must consult—

10.278A.5.a

members of the public in the United Kingdom,

10.278A.5.b

providers of licensed public service channels who are likely to be affected if
the Secretary of State accepts the recommendation, and

10.278A.5.c

such other persons providing television programme services or on-demand
programme services as OFCOM consider appropriate.

10.278A.6

Before making regulations under  subsection (1) , the Secretary of State must
consult the following persons about their content—

10.278A.6.a

OFCOM,

10.278A.6.b

providers of licensed public service channels who are likely to be affected by
the regulations, and

10.278A.6.c

such other persons providing television programme services or on-demand
programme services as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

10.278A.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  subsection (1)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

10.278A.8

See also sections  278B  and  278C  (which make further provision for the
interpretation of this section etc).

##### Quotas: meaning of “qualifying audiovisual content” etc

11

After section  278A  of the Communications Act 2003 (as inserted by  section
10 ) insert—

######### Quotas: meaning of “qualifying audiovisual content” etc

11.278B

11.278B.1

In this Part, “ qualifying audiovisual content ” means any material, other
than advertisements, included in a qualifying audiovisual service.

11.278B.2

For the purposes of this Part, a person makes available qualifying audiovisual
content if—

11.278B.2.a

that content is provided by—

11.278B.2.a.i

the person, or

11.278B.2.a.ii

a person associated with the person, under arrangements made between the
person and that associated person,

by means of a qualifying audiovisual service provided by the person or (as the
case may be) that associated person,

11.278B.2.b

that content, and the qualifying audiovisual service by means of which it is
provided, may be received or accessed in intelligible form and free of charge,
and

11.278B.2.c

where the qualifying audiovisual service in question is an on-demand programme
service, that content is available for the period described in section 264
(8B)  unless it is excepted by section 264 (8C) .

11.278B.3

Where the period described in section 264 (8B)  falls partly in one year and
partly in another year, the person is to be regarded for the purposes of this
Part as making the qualifying audiovisual content available in the year in
which the period begins.

11.278B.4

Section  362AZ12 (6)  (meaning of references to a person associated with a
public service broadcaster) applies for the purposes of  subsection (2) (a) as
it applies for the purposes of Part 3A.

11.278B.5

Subsection  (8A)  of section 264 applies for the purposes of  subsection (2)
(b)  as it applies for the purposes of  subsection (8)  of that section.

11.278B.6

For the purposes of this Part, the following are qualifying audiovisual
services—

11.278B.6.a

television broadcasting services;

11.278B.6.b

on-demand programme services that are, or form part of, designated internet
programme services;

11.278B.6.c

any other service that—

11.278B.6.c.i

is a relevant audiovisual service for the purposes of section 264 (see section
264 (11) ), and

11.278B.6.c.ii

is specified, or falls within a description specified, in regulations made by
the Secretary of State.

11.278B.7

In relation to a qualifying audiovisual service that is an on-demand programme
service, references in this Part to “ provide ” (and related expressions) are
to be read in accordance with section 368R(5).

11.278B.8

Before making regulations under  subsection (6) (c) , the Secretary of State
must consult OFCOM.

11.278B.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  subsection (6) (c)  may
not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved
by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

11.278B.10

In this section, “ designated internet programme service ” has the same
meaning as in Part 3A (see  section 362AZ12 ).

##### Quotas: further provision about their fulfilment

12

After section  278B  of the Communications Act 2003 (as inserted by  section
11 ) insert—

######### Quotas: further provision about their fulfilment

12.278C

12.278C.1

In this section, a “ quota condition ” means—

12.278C.1.a

a condition that forms part of the regulatory regime of a licensed public
service channel by virtue of—

12.278C.1.a.i

section 277 (1)  or (4) (quotas for independent productions),

12.278C.1.a.ii

section 278 (1)  (quotas for original productions),

12.278C.1.a.iii

section 278A (4)  (additional quotas), or

12.278C.1.a.iv

section 286(1)(a) and (aa) or (3)(a) and (aa) or 288(1)(a) and (aa) (regional
programme-making quotas relating to duration);

12.278C.1.b

a condition that forms part of the regulatory regime of a licensed public
service channel by virtue of section 286(1)(c) or (3)(c) or 288(1)(c)
(regional programme-making quotas relating to expenditure), where the
condition is framed by reference to the making available of qualifying
audiovisual content;

12.278C.1.c

a duty of the BBC under or by virtue of paragraph 1(1) or (4) of Schedule 12
(BBC quotas for independent productions);

12.278C.1.d

a duty of S4C under or by virtue of paragraph 7(1) or (4) or 8(1) of Schedule
12 (S4C quotas for independent productions and original productions).

12.278C.2

The Secretary of State must by regulations make provision determining whether
qualifying audiovisual content that is made available by a person in the
circumstances described in subsection (3) may be counted towards meeting a
quota condition.

12.278C.3

Those circumstances are that the person has previously made available
audiovisual content consisting of the same or substantially the same material
(whether in the same year or a previous year).

12.278C.4

For the purposes of subsection (3)—

12.278C.4.a

“ audiovisual content ” has the same meaning as in section 264;

12.278C.4.b

section 264 (13)  (interpretation of “made available”) applies as it applies
for the purposes of section 264.

12.278C.5

Except in the case of a quota condition relating to independent productions,
regulations under subsection (2) may, instead of determining the matter
described in that subsection, require OFCOM to determine it.

12.278C.6

Where the regulations require OFCOM to determine the matter, OFCOM must do so—

12.278C.6.a

in relation to a quota condition falling within  subsection (1) (a)  or  (b) ,
by conditions included in the licence of the provider of the licensed public
service channel, and

12.278C.6.b

in relation to a quota condition falling within  subsection (1) (d) , by a
direction given by OFCOM to S4C.

12.278C.7

Before giving a direction under  subsection (6) (b) , OFCOM must consult S4C.

12.278C.8

In relation to a quota condition falling within  subsection (1) (a)  or  (b) ,
the reference in  subsection (3)  to the person includes a reference to any
person who previously held the licence to provide the licensed public service
channel in question.

12.278C.9

Before making regulations under  subsection (2) , the Secretary of State must
consult OFCOM.

12.278C.10

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  subsection (2)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

#### Information

##### Power to require information

18

After section 338 of the Communications Act 2003 insert—

######### Information relating to certain OFCOM functions

########## Power to require information

18.338A

18.338A.1

OFCOM may by notice (an “information notice”) require a person within
subsection (4)  to provide them with any information that they require for the
purpose of carrying out their functions under—

18.338A.1.a

sections 198B to 198D,

18.338A.1.b

sections 263 to 294 and Schedule 11, and

18.338A.1.c

paragraphs 5 and 7 to 10 of Schedule 12.

18.338A.2

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  includes power to require a person
within  subsection (4)  to obtain or generate information.

18.338A.3

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  must be exercised in a way that is
proportionate to the use to which the information is to be put by OFCOM.

18.338A.4

The persons within this subsection are—

18.338A.4.a

a provider of a licensed public service channel;

18.338A.4.b

S4C;

18.338A.4.c

a person with whom a public service broadcaster has made such arrangements as
are referred to in section 264 (13) (b) ;

18.338A.4.d

a person who is not within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  but who provides a
media service (within the meaning of section 264A);

18.338A.4.e

a person who was within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (d)  at a time to which
the required information relates;

18.338A.4.f

a person who is not within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (e)  but who appears to
OFCOM to have, or to be able to obtain or generate, information required by
them as mentioned in  subsection (1) .

18.338A.5

An information notice must—

18.338A.5.a

specify or describe the information to be provided,

18.338A.5.b

specify why OFCOM require the information,

18.338A.5.c

specify the form and manner in which the information must be provided, and

18.338A.5.d

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice.

18.338A.6

An information notice must specify when the information must be provided which
may be—

18.338A.6.a

on or by a specified date, or

18.338A.6.b

within a specified period.

18.338A.7

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  to require the provision of
information includes power to require the provision of information held
outside the United Kingdom.

18.338A.8

OFCOM may not use the power conferred by  subsection (1)  to require the BBC
to provide, obtain or generate information.

18.338A.9

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  does not include power to require the
provision of information in respect of which a claim to legal professional
privilege, or (in Scotland) to confidentiality of communications, could be
maintained in legal proceedings.

18.338A.10

A person to whom an information notice is given must provide the information
in accordance with any requirements included in the notice (subject to
subsection (11) ).

18.338A.11

The duty under  subsection (10)  does not require a disclosure of information
if that disclosure would contravene the data protection legislation (but, in
determining whether a disclosure would do so, that duty is to be taken into
account).

18.338A.12

In this section—

      “ data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);           “ public service
broadcaster ” has the meaning given by section 264.

########## Penalties for failure to provide information

18.338B

18.338B.1

This section applies if—

18.338B.1.a

OFCOM have given an information notice under  section 338A  to a person within
section 338A (4) , and

18.338B.1.b

OFCOM have determined, after giving the person an opportunity to make
representations, that there are reasonable grounds for believing that there
was, or is, a failure by the person to comply with the information notice.

18.338B.2

OFCOM may give the person a notice (a “penalty notice”) requiring the person
to pay OFCOM a penalty of an amount specified in the notice.

18.338B.3

The penalty may include an amount for each day on which the person fails to
comply with the information notice.

18.338B.4

The amount of the penalty under  subsection (2)  is to be such amount, not
exceeding £250,000, as OFCOM determine to be—

18.338B.4.a

appropriate; and

18.338B.4.b

proportionate to the failure to comply in respect of which it is imposed.

18.338B.5

If the penalty notice is given in relation to a continuing failure to comply
with the information notice, the penalty notice may also require the person to
pay OFCOM a penalty of an amount specified in the penalty notice in respect of
each day after the giving of the penalty notice on which the failure
continues.

18.338B.6

The amount of a penalty under  subsection (5)  is to be such amount, not
exceeding £500 per day, as OFCOM determine to be—

18.338B.6.a

appropriate; and

18.338B.6.b

proportionate to the failure to comply in respect of which it is imposed.

18.338B.7

A penalty notice must—

18.338B.7.a

fix a reasonable period after it is given as the period within which a penalty
under  subsection (2)  is to be paid;

18.338B.7.b

where penalties under  subsection (5)  are imposed, fix a reasonable period as
the period within which such a penalty is to be paid.

18.338B.8

A financial penalty imposed under this section must be paid to OFCOM within
the period fixed by them.

#### Amount of financial penalties

##### Amount of financial penalties: qualifying revenue

19

19.1

The Broadcasting Act 1990 is amended as set out in subsections  (2)  to  (5) .

19.2

In section 18 (failure to begin providing licensed Channel 3 service and
financial penalties on revocation of Channel 3 licence), in subsection (3D),
for “Section 19(2) to (6)” substitute  “Section  18A ” .

19.3

After section 18 insert—

########### Section 18: supplementary provision

19.3.18A

19.3.18A.1

For the purposes of section 18(3B) or (3C), the qualifying revenue for an
accounting period of a holder of a Channel 3 licence is the aggregate of—

19.3.18A.1.a

the qualifying revenue for that accounting period of the licence holder which
derives from that licensed service, and

19.3.18A.1.b

the qualifying revenue for that accounting period of the licence holder which
derives from any on-demand programme service, non-UK on-demand programme
service or television programme service that is—

19.3.18A.1.b.i

provided by the licence holder or a person associated with the licence holder,
and

19.3.18A.1.b.ii

included in an internet programme service that is designated under  section
362AA (2)  of the Communications Act 2003 as a service provided by the licence
holder or as a service provided by a person associated with the licence
holder.

19.3.18A.2

Section 19(2) to (6) applies for determining the qualifying revenue referred
to in  subsection (1) (a) .

19.3.18A.3

Section 368J(4), (5) and (7) of the Communications Act 2003 applies for
determining the qualifying revenue referred to in  subsection (1) (b)  which
derives from an on-demand programme service or a non-UK on-demand programme
service.

19.3.18A.4

Section 19(2) and (4) to (6) applies for determining the qualifying revenue
referred to in  subsection (1) (b)  which derives from a television programme
service as if—

19.3.18A.4.a

in section 19(2) and (6), references to a Channel 3 service were references to
the television programme service,

19.3.18A.4.b

in section 19(2), (4) and (6), references to the holder of a Channel 3 licence
were references to the provider of the television programme service, and

19.3.18A.4.c

in section 19(2) and (6), the words “of the licence holder” were omitted.

19.3.18A.5

Section  362AZ12 (6)  of the Communications Act 2003 (meaning of references to
a person associated with a public service broadcaster) applies for the
purposes of this section as it applies for the purposes of Part 3A of that
Act.

19.3.18A.6

For the purposes of this section—

19.3.18A.6.a

the person who provides an internet programme service is the person treated
for the purposes of Part 3A of the Communications Act 2003 as providing that
service (see  section 362AZ12  of that Act), and

19.3.18A.6.b

the person who provides an on-demand programme service or a non-UK on-demand
programme service is the person treated for the purposes of Part 4A of that
Act as providing that service (see section 368R of that Act).

19.3.18A.7

In this section—

      “ designated internet programme service ” has the same meaning as in
Part 3A of the Communications Act 2003 (see  section 362AZ12 (1) );
“ on-demand programme service ” and “non-UK on-demand programme service” have
the same meaning as in Part 4A of that Act (see section 368A).

19.4

In section 41 (power to impose financial penalty or shorten licence period of
a Channel 3 service, Channel 4 and Channel 5), for subsection (1C) substitute—

19.4.1C

Section  18A  applies for determining or estimating qualifying revenue for the
purposes of subsection (1A) or (1B), with any necessary modifications in
relation to the holder of the Channel 5 licence.

19.5

In Schedule 7 (qualifying revenue: supplementary provisions), in Part 1
(qualifying revenue for the purposes of Part 1 or 2 of this Act), in paragraph
1, after sub-paragraph (4) insert—

19.5.5

This paragraph does not apply in relation to such part of a person’s
qualifying revenue as falls to be ascertained in accordance with section 368J
of the Communications Act 2003 (see  section 18A (1) (b)  and  (3)  of this
Act).

19.6

In Schedule 9 to the Communications Act 2003 (arrangements about the carrying
on of C4C’s activities), in paragraph 8 (penalty for contravention of the
arrangements), for sub-paragraph (7) substitute—

19.6.7

Section  18A  of the 1990 Act, with any necessary modifications, has effect in
relation to C4C for the purposes of this paragraph as it has effect in
relation to the holder of a Channel 3 licence for the purposes of Part 1 of
the 1990 Act; and Part 1 of Schedule 7 to the 1990 Act has effect as if C4C’s
qualifying revenue for an accounting period were being ascertained for the
purposes of a provision of Part 1 of the 1990 Act.

#### Sporting and other events of national interest

##### Categories of relevant service

20

20.1

Section 98 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (categories of service) is amended as
follows.

20.2

For subsections (1) and (2) substitute—

20.2.1

For the purposes of this Part, relevant services are divided into two
categories as follows—

20.2.1.a

those relevant services which for the time being fall within  subsection (1A)
or  (2A) , and

20.2.1.b

all other relevant services.

20.2.1A

A television programme service falls within this subsection if it is—

20.2.1A.a

a service provided by the BBC or a BBC company otherwise than with a view to
generating a profit,

20.2.1A.b

a Channel 3 service, Channel 4 or Channel 5,

20.2.1A.c

S4C Digital, or

20.2.1A.d

a service, other than a Channel 3 service, Channel 4, Channel 5 or S4C
Digital, which is provided by the provider of one of those services or by a
Channel 4 company, S4C company or body corporate controlled by the provider of
a Channel 3 service or Channel 5,

and it satisfies the conditions in  subsection (2) .

20.2.2

The conditions in this subsection are—

20.2.2.a

that the television programme service may be received free of charge;

20.2.2.b

that, in the case of a service described in  subsection (1A) (d) , the
provider’s latest statement of programme policy under—

20.2.2.b.i

section 266 or 267 of the Communications Act 2003, or

20.2.2.b.ii

paragraph 4 of Schedule 12 to that Act,

states that the service will be used to fulfil the public service remit for
the Channel 3 service, Channel 4 or Channel 5 or (as the case may be) S4C’s
public service remit.

20.2.2A

A relevant service falls within this subsection if—

20.2.2A.a

it is or forms part of a designated internet programme service,

20.2.2A.b

where it is a service that forms part of a designated internet programme
service, it satisfies the conditions in  subsection (2B) , and

20.2.2A.c

it and the programmes included in it may be accessed free of charge.

20.2.2B

The conditions are—

20.2.2B.a

that the relevant service is provided by—

20.2.2B.a.i

the BBC or a person associated with the BBC otherwise than with a view to
generating a profit,

20.2.2B.a.ii

the provider of a Channel 3 service, Channel 4 or Channel 5,

20.2.2B.a.iii

S4C, or

20.2.2B.a.iv

a person associated with a broadcaster mentioned in  sub-paragraph (ii)  or
(iii) ;

20.2.2B.b

that, where it is provided by the BBC or a person associated with the BBC, the
service contributes to the promotion of one or more of the BBC’s public
purposes;

20.2.2B.c

that, where it is provided by a broadcaster referred to in  paragraph (a) (ii)
or  (iii)  or a person associated with such a broadcaster, the broadcaster’s
latest statement of programme policy under—

20.2.2B.c.i

section 266 or 267 of the Communications Act 2003, or

20.2.2B.c.ii

paragraph 4 of Schedule 12 to that Act,

states that the service will be used to fulfil the public service remit for
the Channel 3 service, Channel 4 or Channel 5 or (as the case may be) S4C’s
public service remit.

20.2.2C

Where a relevant service would satisfy the conditions in  subsection (2A)  but
for access to some of the programmes included in the service not being free of
charge—

20.2.2C.a

so much of the service as includes programmes that may be accessed free of
charge, and

20.2.2C.b

the remainder of the service,

are to be regarded as separate relevant services for the purposes of this
Part.

20.2.2D

Section 362AZ12 (6)  of the Communications Act 2003 (meaning of references to
a person associated with a public service broadcaster) applies for the
purposes of  subsection (2B)  as it applies for the purposes of Part 3A of
that Act.

20.3

In subsection (3) (disregard of TV licence fee), after “subsection (2)(a)”
insert  “,  (2A)  or  (2C) ” .

20.4

At the end insert—

20.4.7

In this Part, “ relevant service ” means—

20.4.7.a

a television programme service;

20.4.7.b

an on-demand programme service;

20.4.7.c

a non-UK on-demand programme service;

20.4.7.d

a service, or a dissociable section of a service, which has the following
characteristics—

20.4.7.d.i

its principal purpose is the provision of programmes;

20.4.7.d.ii

the programmes it provides are accessed by means of the internet;

20.4.7.d.iii

there is a person who has general control over what programmes are included in
the service or the dissociable section of the service (see  subsection (8) );

20.4.7.d.iv

it is made available by that person for use by members of the public;

20.4.7.d.v

the members of the public who use the service, or the dissociable section of
the service, are or include members of the public in the United Kingdom;

20.4.7.d.vi

it is not a television programme service, on-demand programme service or non-
UK on-demand programme service;

20.4.7.d.vii

it is not a service of the kind described in  section 362AA (10) (c)  of the
Communications Act 2003 (internet programme services which provide programmes
by means of an on-demand programme service or non-UK on-demand programme
service and at least one other service).

20.4.8

The person by reference to whom the requirement in  subsection (7) (d) (iii)
is satisfied need not have control of the contents of individual programmes or
of the distribution of the service.

20.4.9

In this section, “ programme ” means such programme as is described in section
368ZA of the Communications Act 2003.

##### Contracts relating to coverage of listed events

21

21.1

Section 99 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (contract for exclusive right to
televise listed event to be void) is amended as set out in subsections  (2)
and  (3) .

21.2

For subsection (1) substitute—

21.2.1

Any contract entered into on or after the day on which  section 21  of the
Media Act 2024 comes into force which grants rights to include in a relevant
service live coverage of the whole or any part of a Group A event for
reception in, or in order to be accessed by members of the public in, the
United Kingdom or any area of the United Kingdom is void so far as it
purports—

21.2.1.a

in relation to the whole or any part of the event, or

21.2.1.b

in relation to reception, or access by means of the internet, in the United
Kingdom or any part of the United Kingdom,

to grant those rights exclusively.

21.3

For subsection (3) substitute—

21.3.3

For the purposes of this section, rights for a relevant service (“the first
service”) to include live coverage of all or part of a Group A event in that
service for reception in, or in order to be accessed by members of the public
in, the United Kingdom or any area of the United Kingdom are granted
exclusively if the person granting them—

21.3.3.a

has not granted such rights to include live coverage of the whole or, as the
case may be, that part of the event in one or more other relevant services as
are sufficient to authorise, in accordance with  section 101 (2)  or  (3)  or,
as the case may be,  section 101 (4) , the inclusion in the first service of
the live coverage in question, and

21.3.3.b

is precluded by the terms of the contract from doing so.

21.4

Section 100 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (contract for televising listed event
must specify category of service) is amended as set out in subsections  (5)
and  (6) .

21.5

For subsection (1) substitute—

21.5.1

Any contract entered into on or after the day on which  section 21  of the
Media Act 2024 comes into force is void so far as it purports to grant rights
to include live coverage of the whole or any part of a listed event in a
relevant service for reception in, or in order to be accessed by members of
the public in, the United Kingdom, or any area of the United Kingdom, unless
the contract complies with subsection (2).

21.6

In subsection (2)—

21.6.a

for “the television programme provider” substitute  “the provider of the
relevant service” ;

21.6.b

in paragraph (a), for “television programme service” substitute  “relevant
service” ;

21.6.c

in paragraph (b), for “television programme service” substitute  “relevant
service” .

##### Restriction on showing live coverage of listed events

22

For section 101 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (restriction on televising of
listed event) substitute—

######### Restriction on showing live coverage

22.101

22.101.1

A provider of a relevant service who—

22.101.1.a

is providing a relevant service (“the first service”) falling within either
category, and

22.101.1.b

is providing it with a view to its being available to members of the public in
the United Kingdom or in any area of the United Kingdom,

must not include live coverage of a listed event in that service unless it is
authorised by subsection  (2) ,  (3) ,  (4) ,  (5)  or  (6) .

22.101.2

Live coverage of a listed event is authorised by this subsection if—

22.101.2.a

identical rights to include live coverage of the event in a relevant service
other than the first service (“the second service”) have been acquired, and

22.101.2.b

the second service—

22.101.2.b.i

is provided by a person other than the provider of the first service,

22.101.2.b.ii

falls into a different category from the first service,

22.101.2.b.iii

is not a relevant service other than the first service only because section 98
(2C)  applies to it, and

22.101.2.b.iv

is provided for an area that consists of or includes all or almost all of the
area for which the first service is provided.

22.101.3

Live coverage of a listed event is authorised by this subsection if—

22.101.3.a

rights to include live coverage of the event in two or more relevant services
other than the first service (“the second and further services”) have been
acquired,

22.101.3.b

those rights, taken together, constitute identical rights to include live
coverage of the event in the second and further services,

22.101.3.c

each of the second and further services—

22.101.3.c.i

is provided by a person other than the provider of the first service,

22.101.3.c.ii

falls into a different category from the first service,

22.101.3.c.iii

is not a relevant service other than the first service only because section 98
(2C)  applies to it, and

22.101.3.c.iv

is provided for an area that consists of or includes all or almost all of the
area for which the first service is provided.

22.101.4

Live coverage of a listed event is authorised by this subsection if—

22.101.4.a

the event is a sporting event that involves different sports,

22.101.4.b

rights to include live coverage of the event in two or more relevant services
other than the first service (“the second and further services”) have been
acquired,

22.101.4.c

that additional coverage, taken as a whole, is adequate live coverage of the
event,

22.101.4.d

at least two of the second and further services are television programme
services, and

22.101.4.e

each of the second and further services—

22.101.4.e.i

is provided by a person other than the provider of the first service,

22.101.4.e.ii

falls into a different category from the first service,

22.101.4.e.iii

is not a relevant service other than the first service only because section 98
(2C)  applies to it, and

22.101.4.e.iv

is provided for an area that consists of or includes all or almost all of the
area for which the first service is provided.

22.101.5

Live coverage of a listed event is authorised by this subsection if OFCOM have
consented in advance to inclusion of that coverage in the first service.

22.101.6

Live coverage of a listed event is authorised by this subsection if—

22.101.6.a

the listed event is a Group B event,

22.101.6.b

rights to provide coverage of the event have been acquired by one or more
persons in addition to the provider of the first service,

22.101.6.c

that additional coverage constitutes adequate alternative coverage of the
event, and

22.101.6.d

the person or persons who have acquired rights to provide the additional
coverage satisfy the requirements in relation to that coverage of any
regulations made under section 104ZA for the purposes of this paragraph.

22.101.7

Subsections  (1)  to  (6)  apply in relation to the coverage of a part of a
listed event as they apply in relation to the coverage of the whole of that
event.

22.101.8

OFCOM may revoke any consent given by them for the purposes of  subsection (5)
.

22.101.9

Failure to comply with  subsection (1)  does not affect the validity of any
contract.

22.101.10

Subsection (1)  does not have effect where the person providing the first
service is exercising rights acquired before the commencement of  section 22
of the Media Act 2024.

22.101.11

References in this section to a category of service are to a category of
service set out in section 98 (1) .

##### Regulations about coverage of listed events

23

23.1

Section 104ZA of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (regulations about coverage of
listed events) is amended as follows.

23.2

In subsection (1)—

23.2.a

in paragraph (a)—

23.2.a.i

for “televising” substitute  “coverage” ;

23.2.a.ii

after “live” insert  “coverage” ;

23.2.b

after paragraph (a) insert—

23.2.b.aa

what (whether generally or in relation to particular circumstances) is to be
taken to represent the provision of adequate live coverage for the purposes of
section 101(4)(c);

;

23.2.c

in paragraph (b), after “coverage” insert  “for the purposes of  section 101
(6) (c) ” ;

23.2.d

in paragraph (c), for “section 101(1C)(d)” substitute  “ section 101 (6) (d) ”
.

23.3

In subsection (2), for ““live”” substitute  ““live coverage”” .

23.4

After subsection (2) insert—

23.4.2A

Regulations made by virtue of subsection (1)(aa) may, in particular—

23.4.2A.a

describe what represents the provision of adequate live coverage by reference
to—

23.4.2A.a.i

the duration of the live coverage (whether expressed as a percentage of the
duration of the proceedings or otherwise),

23.4.2A.a.ii

the numbers of relevant services of particular descriptions in which the live
coverage is included (subject to  section 101 (4) (d) ), or

23.4.2A.a.iii

a combination of those matters;

23.4.2A.b

provide for live coverage not to be taken into account if the provider of the
service is unable to select what parts of the proceedings are covered.

23.4.2B

When making regulations by virtue of subsection (1)(aa), OFCOM must have
regard to—

23.4.2B.a

the forms of live coverage that OFCOM consider are likely to satisfy the
interest of members of the public in the United Kingdom or an area of the
United Kingdom in listed events of the sort to which section 101(4)(c)
relates;

23.4.2B.b

the desirability of facilitating the making of arrangements under which rights
to include live coverage of sporting events that involve different sports are
acquired by providers of relevant services in both of the categories of
relevant service set out in section 98(1).

##### Provision of information

24

24.1

Section 104A of the Broadcasting Act 1996 (provision of information) is
amended as set out in subsections  (2)  to  (4) .

24.2

Renumber subsection (2) as subsection (12).

24.3

Before subsection (12) (as renumbered by  subsection (2) ) insert—

24.3.2

OFCOM may by notice (an “information notice”) require a person within
subsection (5)  to provide them with any information that they require for the
purpose of carrying out their functions under this Part relating to listed
events.

24.3.3

The power conferred by  subsection (2)  includes power to require a person
within  subsection (5)  to obtain or generate information.

24.3.4

The power conferred by  subsection (2)  must be exercised in a way that is
proportionate to the use to which the information is to be put by OFCOM.

24.3.5

The persons within this subsection are—

24.3.5.a

a provider of a relevant service;

24.3.5.b

a person who was a provider of a relevant service at a time to which the
required information relates;

24.3.5.c

a person who is not within  paragraph (a)  or  (b)  but who appears to OFCOM
to have, or to be able to obtain or generate, information required by them as
mentioned in  subsection (2) .

24.3.6

An information notice must—

24.3.6.a

specify or describe the information to be provided,

24.3.6.b

specify why OFCOM require the information,

24.3.6.c

specify the form and manner in which the information must be provided, and

24.3.6.d

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice.

24.3.7

An information notice must specify when the information must be provided which
may be—

24.3.7.a

on or by a specified date, or

24.3.7.b

within a specified period.

24.3.8

The power conferred by  subsection (2)  to require the provision of
information includes power to require the provision of information held
outside the United Kingdom.

24.3.9

The power conferred by  subsection (2)  does not include power to require the
provision of information in respect of which a claim to legal professional
privilege, or (in Scotland) to confidentiality of communications, could be
maintained in legal proceedings.

24.3.10

A person to whom an information notice is given must provide the information
in accordance with any requirements included in the notice (subject to
subsection (11) ).

24.3.11

The duty under  subsection (10)  does not require a disclosure of information
if that disclosure would contravene the data protection legislation (but, in
determining whether a disclosure would do so, that duty is to be taken into
account).

24.4

After subsection (12) (as renumbered by  subsection (2) ) insert—

24.4.13

In this section, “ data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in
the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

24.5

After that section insert—

########### Penalties for failure to provide information

24.5.104B

24.5.104B.1

This section applies if—

24.5.104B.1.a

OFCOM have given an information notice under section 104A (2)  to a person
within section 104A (5) , and

24.5.104B.1.b

OFCOM have determined, after giving the person an opportunity to make
representations, that there are reasonable grounds for believing that there
was, or is, a failure by the person to comply with the information notice.

24.5.104B.2

OFCOM may give the person a notice (a “penalty notice”) requiring the person
to pay OFCOM a penalty of an amount specified in the notice.

24.5.104B.3

The penalty may include an amount for each day on which the person fails to
comply with the information notice.

24.5.104B.4

The amount of the penalty under  subsection (2)  is to be such amount, not
exceeding £250,000, as OFCOM determine to be—

24.5.104B.4.a

appropriate; and

24.5.104B.4.b

proportionate to the failure to comply in respect of which it is imposed.

24.5.104B.5

If the penalty notice is given in relation to a continuing failure to comply
with the information notice, the penalty notice may also require the person to
pay OFCOM a penalty of an amount specified in the penalty notice in respect of
each day after the giving of the penalty notice on which the failure
continues.

24.5.104B.6

The amount of a penalty under  subsection (5)  is to be such amount, not
exceeding £500 per day, as OFCOM determine to be—

24.5.104B.6.a

appropriate; and

24.5.104B.6.b

proportionate to the failure to comply in respect of which it is imposed.

24.5.104B.7

A penalty notice must—

24.5.104B.7.a

fix a reasonable period after it is given as the period within which a penalty
under  subsection (2)  is to be paid;

24.5.104B.7.b

where penalties under  subsection (5)  are imposed, fix a reasonable period as
the period within which such a penalty is to be paid.

24.5.104B.8

A financial penalty imposed under this section must be paid to OFCOM within
the period fixed by them.

24.5.104B.9

Where OFCOM receive an amount payable to them by virtue of  subsection (8) ,
that amount is to be paid into the Consolidated Fund.

24.5.104B.10

An amount payable by a person to OFCOM by virtue of  subsection (8)  is
recoverable by OFCOM as a debt due to OFCOM from that person.

##### Sections 

25

25.1

An amendment made by sections  20  to  23  or paragraphs  12  to  19  of
Schedule 2  does not affect the validity of a contract entered into before
sections  20  to  23  come into force or the exercise of rights acquired under
such a contract.

25.2

On the date on which  section 21  comes into force, the Secretary of State
must revise the list maintained for the purposes of Part 4 of the Broadcasting
Act 1996 in order to allocate each event which is a listed event on that date
either to Group A or Group B.

25.3

Where—

25.3.a

the events listed in the list in force immediately before the Secretary of
State revises it under  subsection (2)  are treated, for any of the purposes
of the code in force under section 104 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 at that
time, as divided into two categories, and

25.3.b

the Secretary of State’s revision under  subsection (2)  makes the same
division,

section 97(2) of the Broadcasting Act 1996 is not to apply in relation to that
revision of the list.

25.4

OFCOM must draw up a code under section 104 of the Broadcasting Act 1996 as
soon as practicable after  paragraph 18  of  Schedule 2  to this Act
(amendments of section 104) comes into force.

25.5

The code drawn up by OFCOM in accordance with  subsection (4)  is not to have
effect in relation to any time before  section 22  of this Act comes into
force.

25.6

Regulations under  section 55 (5)  (transitional, transitory or saving
provision in connection with commencement) may provide for the old section 104
code to continue to have effect in relation to cases specified in the
regulations after the coming into force of the code drawn up by OFCOM in
accordance with  subsection (4) .

25.7

In this section—

      “ OFCOM ” means the Office of Communications;           “ the old
section 104 code ” means the code drawn up under section 104 of the
Broadcasting Act 1996 which is continued in effect by paragraph 51(2) of
Schedule 18 to the Communications Act 2003.

#### Public teletext service

##### Public teletext service

26

In the Communications Act 2003, omit sections 218 to 223 (duty to secure the
provision of a public teletext service etc).

#### Further amendments

##### Further amendments relating to public service television

27

Schedule 2  contains further amendments relating to this Part.

### Prominence on television selection services

#### Prominence on television selection services

28

28.1

In the Communications Act 2003, after Part 3 insert—

########## Prominence on television selection services

########### Designated internet programme services

############ Designation of internet programme services

28.1.362AA

28.1.362AA.1

In this Part, “ designated internet programme service ” means—

28.1.362AA.1.a

an internet programme service provided by the BBC,

28.1.362AA.1.b

an internet programme service provided by a public service broadcaster other
than the BBC and designated by OFCOM under  subsection (2)  for the purposes
of this Part, or

28.1.362AA.1.c

an internet programme service provided by a person associated with a public
service broadcaster and designated by OFCOM as described in  paragraph (b) .

28.1.362AA.2

OFCOM may designate an internet programme service provided by a public service
broadcaster other than the BBC or a person associated with a public service
broadcaster if—

28.1.362AA.2.a

the service satisfies the conditions in  subsection (3) ,  (4)  or  (5)  that
apply to it; and

28.1.362AA.2.b

OFCOM consider that it is appropriate to designate the service.

28.1.362AA.3

The conditions in the case of an internet programme service provided by the
provider of a licensed public service channel or a person associated with the
provider of that licensed public service channel are—

28.1.362AA.3.a

that the service makes or would, if designated, be capable of making—

28.1.362AA.3.a.i

a significant contribution to the fulfilment of the public service remit for
that licensed public service channel, or

28.1.362AA.3.a.ii

in a case where the provider of the service is, in relation to two or more
licensed public service channels, either the provider of, or a person
associated with the provider of, the channels, a significant contribution to
the fulfilment of the public service remit for at least one of those licensed
public service channels; and

28.1.362AA.3.b

that the public service remit content included in the service is readily
discoverable and is promoted by the service.

28.1.362AA.4

The conditions in the case of an internet programme service provided by S4C or
a person associated with S4C are—

28.1.362AA.4.a

that the service makes or would, if designated, be capable of making a
significant contribution to the fulfilment of S4C’s public service remit; and

28.1.362AA.4.b

that the public service remit content included in the service is readily
discoverable and is promoted by the service.

28.1.362AA.5

The conditions in the case of an internet programme service provided by a
person associated with the BBC are—

28.1.362AA.5.a

that the service makes or would, if designated, be capable of making a
significant contribution to the promotion of one or more of the BBC’s public
purposes; and

28.1.362AA.5.b

that the material contributing to the promotion of one or more of those
purposes which is included in the service is readily discoverable and is
promoted by the service.

28.1.362AA.6

In considering whether an internet programme service provided by a person
other than the BBC satisfies the conditions in  subsection (3) ,  (4)  or  (5)
that apply to it, OFCOM must have regard to any statement for the time being
published by OFCOM under  section 362AC .

28.1.362AA.7

In considering whether it is appropriate to designate an internet programme
service provided by a public service broadcaster other than the BBC or a
person associated with such a broadcaster, OFCOM must have regard, in
particular, to the following matters—

28.1.362AA.7.a

any proposals included in any such public service broadcaster’s latest
statement of programme policy published under section 266 or 267 or paragraph
4 of Schedule 12 as to the contribution that the internet programme service
will make towards fulfilling the public service remit for its licensed public
service channel or (as the case may be) S4C’s public service remit;

28.1.362AA.7.b

whether that proposed contribution is capable of satisfying the needs and
interests of—

28.1.362AA.7.b.i

a specific audience, in a case where the service would, if designated, be the
second or further designated internet programme service provided by a public
service broadcaster or a person associated with that broadcaster, or

28.1.362AA.7.b.ii

a wide range of audiences, in any other case;

28.1.362AA.7.c

in relation to any such public service broadcaster whose public service remit
content is included in the internet programme service, how effective and
efficient is the broadcaster’s monitoring of its performance so far as
relating to the fulfilment of the public service remit for its licensed public
service channel or (as the case may be) S4C’s public service remit.

28.1.362AA.8

In considering whether it is appropriate to designate an internet programme
service provided by a person associated with the BBC, OFCOM must have regard,
in particular, to the following matters—

28.1.362AA.8.a

any proposals included in a statement of policy made by the BBC in pursuance
of the BBC Charter and Agreement as to the contribution that the service will
make towards the promotion of one or more of the BBC’s public purposes;

28.1.362AA.8.b

whether that proposed contribution is capable of satisfying the needs and
interests of—

28.1.362AA.8.b.i

a specific audience, in a case where the service would, if designated, be the
second or further designated internet programme service provided by the BBC or
a person associated with the BBC, or

28.1.362AA.8.b.ii

a wide range of audiences, in any other case;

28.1.362AA.8.c

how effective and efficient is the BBC’s monitoring of the contribution of
persons associated with the BBC to the promotion of one or more of the BBC’s
public purposes.

28.1.362AA.9

Before designating an internet programme service, OFCOM must consult—

28.1.362AA.9.a

the provider of the service;

28.1.362AA.9.b

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

28.1.362AA.10

In this Part, a reference to an internet programme service is a reference to—

28.1.362AA.10.a

an on-demand programme service where the programmes viewed by a user of the
service are accessed by the user by means of the internet,

28.1.362AA.10.b

a non-UK on-demand programme service where the programmes viewed by a user of
the service are accessed by the user by means of the internet, or

28.1.362AA.10.c

a service which satisfies the requirements in  subsection (11) .

28.1.362AA.11

The requirements are—

28.1.362AA.11.a

that the principal purpose of the service is the provision of programmes,

28.1.362AA.11.b

that the programmes viewed by a user of the service are accessed by the user
by means of the internet, and

28.1.362AA.11.c

that the programmes it provides to a user of the service are contained in—

28.1.362AA.11.c.i

such on-demand programme service as is described in  subsection (10) (a)  or
such non-UK on-demand programme service as is described in  subsection (10)
(b) , and

28.1.362AA.11.c.ii

another service which is, or two or more other services each of which is, such
an on-demand programme service, such a non-UK on-demand programme service, or
a service (other than those kinds of service) that consists of, or has as its
principal purpose the provision of, programmes.

28.1.362AA.12

In this section—

      “ public service remit ”—         in relation to a Channel 3 service or
Channel 5, has the meaning given by section 265(2);           in relation to
Channel 4, has the meaning given by section 265(3);           in relation to
S4C, has the meaning given by  section 204A ;                 “ public service
remit content ”, in relation to an internet programme service provided by a
public service broadcaster other than the BBC or a person associated with such
a broadcaster, means material included in the internet programme service that
contributes to the fulfilment of—         the public service remit for the
licensed public service channel in question, or           S4C’s public service
remit (as the case may be).

############ Revocation of designation

28.1.362AB

28.1.362AB.1

If an internet programme service provided by a person other than a public
service broadcaster is designated under  section 362AA (2) , the designation
is revoked on the person ceasing to be associated with—

28.1.362AB.1.a

if the person is associated with only one public service broadcaster, that
public service broadcaster, or

28.1.362AB.1.b

if the person is associated with more than one public service broadcaster, all
of those public service broadcasters.

28.1.362AB.2

OFCOM may give notice under  subsection (3)  to a person other than the BBC
who provides a designated internet programme service if OFCOM consider that
there are reasonable grounds for believing that—

28.1.362AB.2.a

a designated internet programme service provided by that person is not making
such contribution as is described in  subsection (3) (a) ,  subsection (4) (a)
or (as the case may be)  subsection (5) (a)  of  section 362AA ,

28.1.362AB.2.b

the content included in the service which is of the description referred to in
subsection (3) (b) ,  subsection (4) (b)  or (as the case may be)  subsection
(5) (b)  of  section 362AA  is not readily discoverable or is not promoted by
the service, or

28.1.362AB.2.c

the service is not a service that it would be appropriate for OFCOM to
designate under  section 362AA (2) .

28.1.362AB.3

A notice under this subsection must—

28.1.362AB.3.a

state that OFCOM consider that there are reasonable grounds for believing the
matter in paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  of  subsection (2) ;

28.1.362AB.3.b

give OFCOM’s reasons for that opinion;

28.1.362AB.3.c

give OFCOM’s reasons for proposing to revoke the designation of the internet
programme service;

28.1.362AB.3.d

state that the person may make representations to OFCOM about the matters
contained in the notice;

28.1.362AB.3.e

specify the period within which such representations may be made.

28.1.362AB.4

Where the period allowed for representations has expired, OFCOM must, after
considering any representations that have been made—

28.1.362AB.4.a

decide whether or not to revoke the designation, and

28.1.362AB.4.b

give notice to the person of their decision.

28.1.362AB.5

Where OFCOM decide to revoke a designation, a notice under  subsection (4) (b)
must—

28.1.362AB.5.a

state that OFCOM are satisfied as to the matter in paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or
(c)  of  subsection (2) ;

28.1.362AB.5.b

give OFCOM’s reasons for being so satisfied.

28.1.362AB.6

In considering whether there are reasonable grounds for believing the matter
in paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  of  subsection (2)  or whether they are
satisfied as to that matter, OFCOM must have regard to any statement for the
time being published by OFCOM under  section 362AC .

28.1.362AB.7

OFCOM must revoke a designation of an internet programme service under
section 362AA (2)  if the person providing the service requests them to do so.

############ Statement relating to designation functions

28.1.362AC

28.1.362AC.1

OFCOM must prepare and publish a statement providing—

28.1.362AC.1.a

information about the methods applied in determining the matters in sections
362AA (3) ,  (4)  and  (5)  and  362AB (2) , and

28.1.362AC.1.b

such other information relating to the determination of those matters as OFCOM
consider appropriate.

28.1.362AC.2

OFCOM may revise or replace a statement published under this section and,
where they do so, must publish the revised or replacement statement.

############ Notifications in relation to designated internet programme services

28.1.362AD

28.1.362AD.1

Where an internet programme service provided by a person associated with a
public service broadcaster has been designated under  section 362AA (2) , the
person must give notice to OFCOM if the person ceases to be a person
associated with that public service broadcaster.

28.1.362AD.2

A notice given to OFCOM under this section must—

28.1.362AD.2.a

be sent in such manner as OFCOM may require;

28.1.362AD.2.b

contain such information as OFCOM may require.

########### Regulated television selection services

############ Meaning of “television selection service”

28.1.362AE

28.1.362AE.1

In this Part, “ television selection service ” means a service or a
dissociable section of a service, provided by means of the internet and in
connection with internet television equipment, which consists of—

28.1.362AE.1.a

the presentation of the internet programme services included in the service or
the dissociable section of the service, and

28.1.362AE.1.b

a facility that enables the user—

28.1.362AE.1.b.i

to make a selection between those services or between programmes provided by
those services or both, and

28.1.362AE.1.b.ii

to access the service selected or the programme selected or both.

28.1.362AE.2

In  subsection (1) , “ internet television equipment ” means any apparatus or
combination of apparatus specified in regulations made by the Secretary of
State setting out the descriptions of apparatus or combinations of apparatus
that are internet television equipment for the purposes of this Part.

28.1.362AE.3

Regulations made by virtue of  subsection (2)  may—

28.1.362AE.3.a

provide for references to internet television equipment to include references
to software used in association with apparatus, and

28.1.362AE.3.b

describe apparatus or a combination of apparatus by reference to software used
in association with the apparatus or any of it.

28.1.362AE.4

Exceptions in regulations made by virtue of  subsection (2)  may include
exceptions relating to the purpose or purposes for which a description of
apparatus may be used in addition to the purpose of viewing internet programme
services.

28.1.362AE.5

The person, and the only person, who is to be treated for the purposes of this
Part as providing a television selection service is the person who has general
control over the manner in which the service presents to its users the
internet programme services that are included in the service.

28.1.362AE.6

The fact that a television selection service relies to any extent on
algorithms to determine the prominence given to—

28.1.362AE.6.a

an internet programme service included in the service, or

28.1.362AE.6.b

any programme provided by an internet programme service included in the
service,

does not prevent a person from having general control as described in
subsection (5) .

28.1.362AE.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

28.1.362AE.7.a

amend this section so as to alter the definition of “television selection
service” or “internet television equipment”, and

28.1.362AE.7.b

make such amendments or repeals of any provision of this Act or any other Act
as appear to the Secretary of State to be expedient in consequence of the
amendments made by virtue of  paragraph (a) .

28.1.362AE.8

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  subsection (7)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

############ Meaning of “regulated television selection service”

28.1.362AF

28.1.362AF.1

In this Part, “ regulated television selection service ” means a television
selection service which—

28.1.362AF.1.a

is for the time being designated by regulations made by the Secretary of
State, or

28.1.362AF.1.b

is of a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State.

28.1.362AF.2

The Secretary of State may not exercise the power under  subsection (1) (a)
so as to cause a television selection service to become a regulated television
selection service unless the Secretary of State considers that the service is
used by a significant number of members of the public in the United Kingdom.

28.1.362AF.3

Regulations under  subsection (1) (b)  may, in particular, frame a description
of television selection services by reference to—

28.1.362AF.3.a
